href="/wiki/Santa_Olaya,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santa Olaya, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Santa Olaya</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th colspan="2" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_22" title="Puerto Rico Highway 22"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/PR_primary_22.svg/25px-PR_primary_22.svg.png" decoding="async" scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.municipiodebayamon.com">municipiodebayamon.com</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Bayam\xc3\xb3n</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;ba\xca\x9da\xcb\x88mon&#93;</a></span>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991"><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">locally</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;ba\xca\x9da\xcb\x88mo\xc5\x8b&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_barrio-pueblo" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n barrio-pueblo">city</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and suburb of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> located in the northern coastal valley, north of <a href="/wiki/Aguas_Buenas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguas Buenas, Puerto Rico">Aguas Buenas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comer%C3%ADo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Comer\xc3\xado, Puerto Rico">Comer\xc3\xado</a>; south of <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>; west of <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>; and east of <a href="/wiki/Toa_Alta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Alta, Puerto Rico">Toa Alta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naranjito,_Puerto_Rico" title="Naranjito, Puerto Rico">Naranjito</a>. Bayam\xc3\xb3n is spread over 11 <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_barrio-pueblo" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n barrio-pueblo">Bayam\xc3\xb3n Pueblo</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Downtown" title="Downtown">downtown</a> area and the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative center">administrative center</a> of the city). It is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> and the second most populous municipality in both the metropolitan area and Puerto Rico.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Timeline of Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Timeline of Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico</a></div> \n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:PORTO_RICO_Bayamon_(NBY_444111).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/PORTO_RICO_Bayamon_%28NBY_444111%29.jpg/220px-PORTO_RICO_Bayamon_%28NBY_444111%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/PORTO_RICO_Bayamon_%28NBY_444111%29.jpg/330px-PORTO_RICO_Bayamon_%28NBY_444111%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/PORTO_RICO_Bayamon_%28NBY_444111%29.jpg/440px-PORTO_RICO_Bayamon_%28NBY_444111%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3436" data-file-height="2168" /></a><figcaption>Postcard from 1903 depicting Bayam\xc3\xb3n.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno people</a>, the indigenous peoples who encountered European explorers and settlers, were the long-time settlers in this area. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonist</a> Juan Ram\xc3\xadrez de Arellano established <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_barrio-pueblo" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n barrio-pueblo">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> settlement on May 22, 1772. Two theories exist about the origin of the name Bayam\xc3\xb3n. According to one, it was named after the local Ta\xc3\xadno chief, <i>Bahamon</i>. The other theory states the name was derived from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> word <i>Bayamongo</i>, which is the native name of the <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_River" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n River">river</a> that runs across this region, implying that Bayam\xc3\xb3n is the area around this main river, which later on became the center of the city\'s development.\n</p><p>In 1821, <a href="/wiki/Marcos_Xiorro" title="Marcos Xiorro">Marcos Xiorro</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">African</a> <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavery in the Americas">slave</a>, planned to lead a revolt against the <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">plantation</a> owners and the Spanish colonial government in Puerto Rico. The slave conspiracy was revealed and suppressed, but Xiorro became a hero among the slaves. He is part of Puerto Rico\'s folklore. Marco Xiorro was owned by Vicente Andino, a militia captain who owned a <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> plantation in Bayam\xc3\xb3n.<sup id="cite_ref-GB_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the United States. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Bayam\xc3\xb3n was 19,940.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city grew considerably during the start of the 20th century. The area became home to numerous factories specializing in textiles, fertilizer, aluminum between 1901 and 1920. During this time the city also became home to financial institutions such as the Puerto Rico Commercial Bank (Banco Comercial de Puerto Rico), the American Colonial Bank, the <a href="/wiki/First_National_City_Bank_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="First National City Bank of New York">First National City Bank of New York</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chase_Bank" title="Chase Bank">Chase Manhattan Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Popular,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Popular, Inc.">Banco Popular de Puerto Rico</a>. This developed and strengthened Bayam\xc3\xb3n\'s economy and turned it into both an industrial and commercial hub. The city\'s infrastructure also developed with the establishment of a bigger sewer system.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city was also host to some of the events of the <a href="/wiki/1979_Pan_American_Games" title="1979 Pan American Games">VIII Pan American Games</a> in 1979.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:171017-F-KA253-0111_(37544294300).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/171017-F-KA253-0111_%2837544294300%29.jpg/220px-171017-F-KA253-0111_%2837544294300%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/171017-F-KA253-0111_%2837544294300%29.jpg/330px-171017-F-KA253-0111_%2837544294300%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/171017-F-KA253-0111_%2837544294300%29.jpg/440px-171017-F-KA253-0111_%2837544294300%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4763" data-file-height="3170" /></a><figcaption>Hurricane Maria relief efforts in Bayam\xc3\xb3n on Oct. 17</figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck Puerto Rico on September 20, 2017, causing large-scale damage and destruction to infrastructure. Numerous landslides occurred in Bayam\xc3\xb3n as a result of the hurricane\'s significant amount of rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In Bayam\xc3\xb3n, around 300 homes were destroyed, and two people were killed by Hurricane Mar\xc3\xada. Many municipal buildings, and the <a href="/wiki/Goya_Foods" title="Goya Foods">Goya Foods</a> factory in Bayam\xc3\xb3n sustained significant damage.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Bayam\xc3\xb3n lies in the Northern Coastal Plain region of Puerto Rico. It is bordered by the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comer%C3%ADo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Comer\xc3\xado, Puerto Rico">Comer\xc3\xado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aguas_Buenas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguas Buenas, Puerto Rico">Aguas Buenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toa_Alta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Alta, Puerto Rico">Toa Alta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naranjito,_Puerto_Rico" title="Naranjito, Puerto Rico">Naranjito</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>. Bayam\xc3\xb3n has a surface area of 43.5 square miles (113.1 km2). The terrain is mostly flat, but it does include some large hills such as La Pe\xc3\xb1a and Vergaras.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Bayam\xc3\xb3n is Puerto Rico\'s second-most populous municipality and is part of the large <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> centered around <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>. Other cities included in the metropolitan area are <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canovanas,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Canovanas, Puerto Rico">Can\xc3\xb3vanas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a>. Bayam\xc3\xb3n is served by the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a>. Despite the city\'s size, it has no weather station.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Water_features">Water features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Water features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The rivers that pass through Bayam\xc3\xb3n include the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Bayam%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Bayam\xc3\xb3n">R\xc3\xado Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Hondo_(Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Hondo (Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Hondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Minillas" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Minillas">R\xc3\xado Minillas</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Bucarabones" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Bucarabones">R\xc3\xado Bucarabones</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Cuesta_Arriba" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Cuesta Arriba">R\xc3\xado Cuesta Arriba</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrios_of_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Barrios_of_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.jpg/220px-Barrios_of_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="281" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Barrios_of_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.jpg/330px-Barrios_of_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Barrios_of_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.jpg/440px-Barrios_of_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1182" data-file-height="1510" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Bayam\xc3\xb3n</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Bayam\xc3\xb3n is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a small barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2010_Census_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Census-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_barrio-pueblo" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n barrio-pueblo">Bayam\xc3\xb3n barrio-pueblo</a><sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Buena Vista, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Buena Vista</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cerro_Gordo,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cerro Gordo, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Cerro Gordo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dajaos,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Dajaos, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Dajaos</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guaraguao_Abajo,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaraguao Abajo, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Guaraguao Abajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guaraguao_Arriba,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaraguao Arriba, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Guaraguao Arriba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hato_Tejas,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hato Tejas, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Hato Tejas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Juan_S%C3%A1nchez,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Juan S\xc3\xa1nchez, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Juan S\xc3\xa1nchez</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Minillas,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Minillas, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Minillas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nuevo,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Nuevo, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Nuevo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1jaros,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="P\xc3\xa1jaros, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">P\xc3\xa1jaros</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Olaya,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santa Olaya, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Santa Olaya</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Bayam\xc3\xb3n: Abra Estrecha, Barriada Vista Alegre, Juan S\xc3\xa1nchez, Nuevo, Bda. Cede\xc3\xb1o in P\xc3\xa1jaros, Collores in Santa Olaya, Corea, Dajaos, El Ch\xc3\xadcharo, Sector Gandul, El Volc\xc3\xa1n, La Cambija, La Caridad, La Morenita, Los Viejitos, Papito, Sergio Reyes, Parcelas Sabanas, and Punta Brava.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/House_of_Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa.jpg/250px-House_of_Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="171" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/House_of_Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa.jpg/375px-House_of_Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/House_of_Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa.jpg/500px-House_of_Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="888" data-file-height="609" /></a><figcaption>House where Jos\xc3\xa9 Celso Barbosa was born</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_la_Serna,_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Puente_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_la_Serna%2C_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/250px-Puente_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_la_Serna%2C_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Puente_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_la_Serna%2C_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/375px-Puente_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_la_Serna%2C_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Puente_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_la_Serna%2C_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/500px-Puente_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_la_Serna%2C_Bayam%C3%B3n%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption>Marqu\xc3\xa9s de la Serna Bridge in Bayam\xc3\xb3n\'s City Center, built in 1869. It is the first metal bridge to have been built in the island, and the only metal arch bridge that exists in Puerto Rico.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Bayam\xc3\xb3n is the site of several notable Puerto Rican landmarks and places of interest. Bayam\xc3\xb3n Central Park is a public park where people gather and relax. Bayamon also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Braulio_Castillo" title="Braulio Castillo">Braulio Castillo</a> Theater, the <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Oller" title="Francisco Oller">Francisco Oller</a> Museum, and the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Celso Barbosa">Jos\xc3\xa9 Celso Barbosa</a> Monument. The <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_City_Hall" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n City Hall">Bayam\xc3\xb3n City Hall</a> building is notable by being built across a major divided highway. While walking through a connecting corridor, right above the road, pedestrians can see passing cars underneath. It is believed to be the only building of its class in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the most popular attractions in Bayam\xc3\xb3n is the <a href="/wiki/Parque_de_las_Ciencias" title="Parque de las Ciencias">Parque de las Ciencias</a>. It is a science-themed park with various exhibitions and attractions. It is located in the middle of <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karstic</a> hills. An observation building on one of the hills provides a good view of the metropolitan area. The building hosts antennas for government and civil communication.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/El_parque_del_tren" class="mw-redirect" title="El parque del tren">El parque del tren</a> was a park featuring what was then <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>\'s only working train. It featured a <a href="/wiki/DC-3" class="mw-redirect" title="DC-3">DC-3</a>, which had been used by <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>. In 2001, the park was dismantled and destroyed in the course of major road construction. What is left of the park is a small plaza for activities and an area for jogging and passive entertainment. The area is now known as "Parque del Nino" or "Children\'s Park".\n</p><p>Shopping is a major tourist activity in Bayam\xc3\xb3n. <a href="/wiki/Plaza_del_Sol_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Plaza del Sol (Puerto Rico)">Plaza del Sol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Rio_Hondo" title="Plaza Rio Hondo">Plaza Rio Hondo</a> are large commercial centers in the city.\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Suspension_bridge" title="Suspension bridge">suspension bridge</a> in Bayam\xc3\xb3n is a pedestrian-only bridge, at the time it was built, it was believed to be one of only three of its kind in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>To stimulate local tourism during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Puerto_Rico" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico">COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> (I\'m Touring) campaign in 2021. The campaign featured a passport book with a page for each municipality. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Voy Turisteando</i></span> Bayam\xc3\xb3n passport page lists <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Centro de Conservaci\xc3\xb3n de Manat\xc3\xades</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Paseo Lineal</i></span> over the Bayam\xc3\xb3n River, and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Ron Del Barrilito</i></span> in the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Hacienda Santa Ana</i></span>, as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Ron del Barrilito located in the Hacienda Santa Ana is the oldest rum distillery in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-Guerrero_2021_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guerrero_2021-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hacienda features a <a href="/wiki/Nature_trail" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature trail">nature trail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Bayam\xc3\xb3n celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in May. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival de la Santa Cruz</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-J.D._2006_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J.D._2006-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Bayam\xc3\xb3n include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Celso_Barbosa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Celso Barbosa">Jos\xc3\xa9 Celso Barbosa</a> Birthday Commemoration \xe2\x80\x93 July</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Tree</a> Lighting Ceremony \xe2\x80\x93 November</li>\n<li>Caminata por la diabetes (Diabetes Walk) \xe2\x80\x93 November</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ramonluisrivera-islanders.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ramonluisrivera-islanders.jpg/250px-Ramonluisrivera-islanders.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ramonluisrivera-islanders.jpg/375px-Ramonluisrivera-islanders.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ramonluisrivera-islanders.jpg/500px-Ramonluisrivera-islanders.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption> The mayor watching the Puerto Rico Islanders at Juan Ramon Loubriel</figcaption></figure>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Orangestarsultra.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Orangestarsultra.jpg/250px-Orangestarsultra.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Orangestarsultra.jpg/375px-Orangestarsultra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Orangestarsultra.jpg/500px-Orangestarsultra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Islanders" title="Puerto Rico Islanders">Puerto Rico Islanders</a> fans at Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There are several professional and amateur sports team based in Bayam\xc3\xb3n. The <a href="/wiki/Vaqueros_de_Bayam%C3%B3n" title="Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n">Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a> are the local basketball team that plays at the <a href="/wiki/Baloncesto_Superior_Nacional" title="Baloncesto Superior Nacional">Baloncesto Superior Nacional</a> league. They are currently the leaders as the team with the most championships in the history of the league (15), the last of which was achieved in 2020. The team\'s host venue is the <a href="/wiki/Coliseo_Rub%C3%A9n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Coliseo Rub\xc3\xa9n Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Coliseo Rub\xc3\xa9n Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a>.\n</p><p>The Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n was also <a href="/wiki/Vaqueros_de_Bayam%C3%B3n_(baseball)" title="Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n (baseball)">the name of the baseball club</a> which played from 1974 through 2003 in the <a href="/wiki/Liga_de_B%C3%A9isbol_Profesional_Roberto_Clemente" title="Liga de B\xc3\xa9isbol Profesional Roberto Clemente">Professional Baseball League of Puerto Rico</a>, and played its home games at <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Loubriel_Stadium" title="Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium">Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium</a>.\n</p><p>The city also has a female <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> team, named the <a href="/wiki/Vaqueras_de_Bayam%C3%B3n" title="Vaqueras de Bayam\xc3\xb3n">Vaqueras de Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>, which plays for the <a href="/wiki/Liga_de_Voleibol_Superior_Femenino" title="Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino">Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino</a>.\n</p><p>Bayam\xc3\xb3n was the home of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Islanders" title="Puerto Rico Islanders">Puerto Rico Islanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_FC" title="Puerto Rico FC">Puerto Rico FC</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League_(2011)" class="mw-redirect" title="North American Soccer League (2011)">North American Soccer League</a>. The teams played at <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Loubriel_Stadium" title="Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium">Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium</a> in Bayam\xc3\xb3n. The city\'s main soccer team, <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n FC">Bayam\xc3\xb3n FC</a>, was founded in 1999, and play at matches at <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_Soccer_Complex" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n Soccer Complex">Bayam\xc3\xb3n Soccer Complex</a>.\n</p><p>The famous <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> fight between <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Arg%C3%BCello" title="Alexis Arg\xc3\xbcello">Alexis Arg\xc3\xbcello</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Escalera" title="Alfredo Escalera">Alfredo Escalera</a> dubbed <a href="/wiki/The_Bloody_Battle_of_Bayamon" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bloody Battle of Bayamon">The Bloody Battle of Bayamon</a> (their first; their equally legendary rematch was held in Rimini, Italy) was held in Bayam\xc3\xb3n in 1978. Also, professional boxers <a href="/wiki/Luis_Del_Valle" title="Luis Del Valle">Luis Del Valle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilfredo_Vazquez" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilfredo Vazquez">Wilfredo Vazquez</a> and Wilfredo Vazquez Jr. are from Bayam\xc3\xb3n. <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Boxing Hall of Fame">International Boxing Hall of Fame</a> member <a href="/wiki/Hector_Camacho" class="mw-redirect" title="Hector Camacho">Hector Camacho</a> was born in Bayamon. Current boxing prospect Jean "Chapito" Rivera is from the Bayamon.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:0 auto; width:100%;">\n<caption><b>Bayam\xc3\xb3n sports teams</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Club\n</th>\n<th>Sport\n</th>\n<th>League\n</th>\n<th>Venue\n</th>\n<th>League Championships\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_FC" 3\xe2\x80\x930</li></ul>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vaqueras_de_Bayam%C3%B3n" title="Vaqueras de Bayam\xc3\xb3n">Vaqueras de Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>\n</td>\n<td>Volleyball\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Liga_de_Voleibol_Superior_Femenino" title="Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino">Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Coliseum" class="mw-redirect" title="Rub\xc3\xa9n Rodr\xc3\xadguez Coliseum">Rub\xc3\xa9n Rodr\xc3\xadguez Coliseum</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Recreation">Recreation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Recreation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The municipal government of Bayam\xc3\xb3n manages a wide variety of recreational programs and recreational facilities for public use. The Onofre Carballeira Sports Complex consists of the <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Loubriel_Stadium" title="Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium">Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Soccer Stadium</a>, home of Puerto Rico\'s only professional soccer team, the <a href="/wiki/Coliseo_Rub%C3%A9n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Coliseo Rub\xc3\xa9n Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Ruben Rodr\xc3\xadguez Coliseum</a>, home of the city\'s male basketball team and female volleyball team, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_J._Frau_Gymnasium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Miguel J. Frau Gymnasium (page does not exist)">Miguel J. Frau Gymnasium</a>. The Rafael Mart\xc3\xadnez Nadal Sports Complex\'s main feature is the Pep\xc3\xadn Cestero indoor court, where much of the city\'s minor league basketball and volleyball major events take place. Also, the Efra\xc3\xadn Calca\xc3\xb1o Alicea Sports Complex located in the Lomas Verdes community is home to much of the track and field and swimming events in the region. The Honda Tennis Center, inaugurated in 2002, is composed of 16 tennis courts and is used by local tennis clubs as well as visitors.\n</p><p>A pioneer in the development of soccer in Puerto Rico, mayor <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Luis_Rivera_Jr." title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Rivera Jr.">Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Rivera Jr.</a> inaugurated the Bayam\xc3\xb3n Soccer Complex in 2011, which consists of three professional soccer fields located off the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_5" title="Puerto Rico Highway 5">PR-5 Highway</a>.\n</p><p>The Paseo del Rio (Paseo Lineal) near the <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_River" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n River">Bayam\xc3\xb3n River</a> is a 6-mile stretch shared by joggers, walkers and cyclists. It is divided in two lanes, one for the bicycles and the other for running or walking. The Rio Bayam\xc3\xb3n Golf Course is located near one of the endpoints of the trail and is home to most golf activity in the region.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Julio_Enrique_Monagas_Park" title="Julio Enrique Monagas Park">Julio Enrique Monagas Park</a> has trails used by mountain bikers to train and compete. It also has cliffs where <a href="/wiki/Rappelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Rappelling">rappelling</a> enthusiasts can practice. Monagas, as the locals refer to it, has <a href="/wiki/Mountain_biking" title="Mountain biking">trails</a> for mountain bike riders of all skill levels. Unpaved roads for beginners, single tracks and very technical single tracks, some of them with downhills. After <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>, the tracks were lost, yet by 2019, most of them had been repaired and reopened.\n</p><p>The city also has many smaller baseball parks, open basketball courts, soccer fields, gymnasiums, and communal centers available to the community.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The founding of the town of Bayam\xc3\xb3n is closely tied to the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>. The products currently grown in Bayam\xc3\xb3n include <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit" title="Grapefruit">grapefruit</a>, sugarcane, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> and vegetables. Bayam\xc3\xb3n was also the site where the first hydraulic <a href="/wiki/Sugar_mill" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar mill">sugar mill</a> on the island was built in 1549.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Business">Business</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Business"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Notable malls are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Plaza_del_Sol_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Plaza del Sol (Puerto Rico)">Plaza del Sol</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plaza_Rio_Hondo" title="Plaza Rio Hondo">Plaza Rio Hondo</a></li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Goya_Foods" title="Goya Foods">Goya Foods</a> has its Puerto Rico offices in Bayam\xc3\xb3n.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. In 1899, the United States conducted its first <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Bayam\xc3\xb3n was 19,940.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop{border-spacing:1px;border:1px solid class=""></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mayors of Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">List of mayors of Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>All municipalities in Puerto Rico are administered by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>, elected every four years. The current mayor of Bayam\xc3\xb3n is <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Luis_Rivera_Jr." title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Rivera Jr.">Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Rivera Jr.</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="New Progressive Party of Puerto Rico">New Progressive Party</a> (PNP). He was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2000">2000 general elections</a>, succeeding his father, <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Luis_Rivera" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Rivera">Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Rivera</a>, after 23 years. For a list of all the mayors of Bayam\xc3\xb3n see "External Links".\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district II">Puerto Rico Senatorial district II</a>, which is represented by two Senators. <a href="/wiki/Migdalia_Padilla" title="Migdalia Padilla">Migdalia Padilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carmelo_R%C3%ADos_Santiago" title="Carmelo R\xc3\xados Santiago">Carmelo R\xc3\xados Santiago</a> have served as District Senators since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The current flag of Bayam\xc3\xb3n features the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_cross_flag" title="Nordic cross flag">Nordic cross</a> found in many <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern European</a> flags and is colored in blue and yellow over a white field. It was embroidered by Gloria M. Le\xc3\xb3n and maintains the design and colors of its coat of arms.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This shield is a symbol and synthesis of the history and the values which distinguish the city of Bayam\xc3\xb3n. The main colors of the shield are blue and silver, representing the waters of the <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_River" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n River">Bayam\xc3\xb3n River</a> and recalling that it was on these banks that the first hydraulic sugarcane refinery of Puerto Rico was established in 1549. The center contains the <a href="/wiki/Christian_cross" title="Christian cross">Holy Cross</a> (Santa Cruz), patron of the first church of the municipality and the name of the old sugarcane refinery "Santa Cruz", which was the historical origin of the town of Bayam\xc3\xb3n. The sugarcane flowers (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">guajana</i></span>) allude directly to the sugarcane industry that is of social and economic importance to the origin and development of Bayam\xc3\xb3n.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The five-tower crown, which is used for cities, was assigned to Bayam\xc3\xb3n as an exception for its extraordinary urban development, the magnitude of its population and for its religious dignity, which will possibly be raised to become Episcopal seat. The motto "IN HOC SIGNO VINCES" makes reference to Emperor <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine</a> when in the 4th century had the vision in which the victory was promised to him if it accepted the <a href="/wiki/Christian_cross" title="Christian cross">cross of Christianity</a> as his banner.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Like all municipalities, public education is administered by <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Education" title="Puerto Rico Department of Education">Puerto Rico Department of Education</a>. Due to its population and location within the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan%E2%80%93Caguas%E2%80%93Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Caguas\xe2\x80\x93Guaynabo metropolitan area">San Juan metropolitan region</a>, Bayam\xc3\xb3n is home to many public and private schools. During the 2014\xe2\x80\x932015 academic year, over 150 public schools ranging from elementary school to high school were located in the Bayam\xc3\xb3n school region. On the other hand, the city is also home to numerous private schools of which most have a religious affiliation. Some of the better known religious private schools include <a href="/wiki/Colegio_De_La_Salle" title="Colegio De La Salle">Colegio De La Salle</a>, Academia Santo Tom\xc3\xa1s de Aquino, Academia Santa Rosa, Colegio Beato Carlos Manuel Rodr\xc3\xadguez, and Academia Disc\xc3\xadpulos de Cristo (non-Catholic). Non-religious schools in the city include Bayam\xc3\xb3n Military Academy and the American School.\n</p><p>Bayam\xc3\xb3n also has many higher-learning institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Bayam%C3%B3n" title="University of Puerto Rico at Bayam\xc3\xb3n">University of Puerto Rico at Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>, which is one of the eleven campuses that comprise the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> public university system. Furthermore, the city is also home to some of the most recognized private universities in the island, such as the <a href="/wiki/Interamerican_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Interamerican University of Puerto Rico">Interamerican University of Puerto Rico</a> and its School of Optometry, <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_Central_University" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n Central University">Bayam\xc3\xb3n Central University</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="American University of Puerto Rico">American University of Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Central_del_Caribe" title="Universidad Central del Caribe">Universidad Central del Caribe</a>, and some community colleges. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_University_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan University (Puerto Rico)">Metropolitan University</a> (Universidad Metropolitana), better known as UMET, has a campus in downtown Bayam\xc3\xb3n.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayam%C3%B3n_Station_of_the_Tren_Urbano.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bayam%C3%B3n_Station_of_the_Tren_Urbano.jpg/230px-Bayam%C3%B3n_Station_of_the_Tren_Urbano.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="153" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bayam%C3%B3n_Station_of_the_Tren_Urbano.jpg/345px-Bayam%C3%B3n_Station_of_the_Tren_Urbano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bayam%C3%B3n_Station_of_the_Tren_Urbano.jpg/460px-Bayam%C3%B3n_Station_of_the_Tren_Urbano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="878" data-file-height="585" /></a><figcaption>Tren Urbano at Bayam\xc3\xb3n Station</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The lone line of the <a href="/wiki/Tren_Urbano" title="Tren Urbano">Tren Urbano</a> of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan metropolitan area">San Juan metropolitan area</a> ends at <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_station" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n station">Bayam\xc3\xb3n station</a>, and three of its stops are located within the city. The <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_station" title="Deportivo station">Deportivo station</a>, located off the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">PR-2</a> Highway, is near the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rosa_Mall_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Santa Rosa Mall (Puerto Rico)">Santa Rosa Mall</a>, the Bayam\xc3\xb3n Court of First Instance, and the Onofre Carballeira Sports Complex which contains the <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Loubriel_Stadium" title="Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium">Juan Ram\xc3\xb3n Loubriel Stadium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Coliseo_Rub%C3%A9n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Coliseo Rub\xc3\xa9n Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Ruben Rodr\xc3\xadguez Coliseum</a>.\n</p><p>The city also has a trolley service with regular routes within <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n_barrio-pueblo" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n barrio-pueblo">Downtown Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>.\n</p><p>There are 77 bridges in Bayam\xc3\xb3n.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Diplomacy">Diplomacy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Diplomacy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Bayam\xc3\xb3n serves as the host city for foreign consular representation in Puerto Rico for the following nations:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span data-sort-value="Iceland"><span class="flagicon"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/21px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="21" height="15" class="mw-file-element" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Iceland.svg/42px-Flag_of_Iceland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="900" /></span></span>&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a></span></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_natives_and_residents">Notable natives and residents</h2><span
